Source Code

These source-code files were from the printout at the MIT Museum, with many thanks to Deborah Douglas, the Museum's Curator of Science and Technology, for releasing it to us. The printout was digitally photographed by Paul Fjeld. A team of volunteers transcribed the source code manually from these images or, where appropriate, modified already-transcribed but similar source Luminary 131 (Apollo 13) source code to agree with the images from the printout. Note that the page images presented online are of reduced quality, and that higher-quality images are available. Report any conversion errors or legibility problems in page images to info@sandroid.org. Notations on the program listing read, in part:

	GAP:  ASSEMBLE REVISION 001 OF AGC PROGRAM LMY99 BY NASA 2021112-061
	20'35 OCT. 28,1968
Note that the date is the date of the printout, not the date of the program revision. 

000002,000002:                                                                                                  #  Copyright:    Public domain.
000003,000003:                                                                                                  #  Filename:     MAIN.agc
000004,000004:                                                                                                  #  Purpose:      The main source file for Luminary 1A, revision 099.
000005,000005:                                                                                                  #                It is part of the source code for the Lunar Module's (LM)
000006,000006:                                                                                                  #                Apollo Guidance Computer (AGC) for Apollo 11.
000007,000007:                                                                                                  #  Assembler:    yaYUL
000008,000008:                                                                                                  #  Contact:      Ron Burkey <info@sandroid.org>.
000009,000009:                                                                                                  #  Website:      www.ibiblio.org/apollo/index.html
000010,000010:                                                                                                  #  Mod history:  2009-05-05 RSB  Adapted from Luminary131/MAIN.agc.
000011,000011: 
000012,000012:                                                                                                  #  The contents of the "Luminary099" files, in general, are
000013,000013:                                                                                                  #  transcribed from a digital images created from a hardcopy of the program
000014,000014:                                                                                                  #  residing at the MIT Museum.  Many thanks to Debbie Douglas of the Museum,
000015,000015:                                                                                                  #  and to Paul Fjeld (who made the images).
000016,000016: 
000017,000017:                                                                                                  #  Notations on this document read, in part:
000018,000018: 
000019,000019:                                                                                                  #        ASSEMBLE REVISION 001 OF AGC PROGRAM LMY99 BY NASA 2021112-061
000020,000020:                                                                                                  #        16:27 JULY 14,1969
000021,000021:                                                                                                  #        [Note that this is the date the hardcopy was made, not the
000022,000022:                                                                                                  #        date of the program revision or the assembly.]
000023,000023:                                                                                                  #        ...
000024,000024:                                                                                                  #        THIS LGC PROGRAM IS INTENDED FOR USE IN THE LM DURING THE MANNED
000025,000025:                                                                                                  #        LUNAR LANDING MISSION OR ANY SUBSET THEREOF.
000026,000026:                                                                                                  #        ...
000027,000027: 
000028,000028:                                                                                                  #  The page images themselves, as reduced in size (and consequently in
000029,000029:                                                                                                  #  quality) to be suitable for online presentation, are available at 
000030,000030:                                                                                                  #  http://www.ibiblio.org/apollo.  If you want to see the (much) higher
000031,000031:                                                                                                  #  quality digital images that Paul actually made, contact info@sandroi.org
000032,000032:                                                                                                  #  directly.
000033,000033: 
000034,000034:                                                                                                  #  This file is a little different from the other Luminary099 files I'm providing, 
000035,000035:                                                                                                  #  in that it doesn't represent anything that appears directly in the original source.  
000036,000036:                                                                                                  #  What I (RSB) have done for organizational purposes is to split the huge monolithic
000037,000037:                                                                                                  #  source code into smaller, more manageable chunks--i.e., into individual source 
000038,000038:                                                                                                  #  files.  Those files are rejoined within this file as "includes".  It just makes
000039,000039:                                                                                                  #  it a little easier to work with.  The code chunks correspond to natural divisions
000040,000040:                                                                                                  #  into sub-programs.  In fact, these divisions are more-or-less specified by
000041,000041:                                                                                                  #  the source code itself.  Refer to the "TABLE OF SUBROUTINE LOG SECTIONS" at the
000042,000042:                                                                                                  #  very beginning of the file ASSEMBLY_AND_OPERATION_INFORMATION.agc.
000043,000043: 
000044,000044:                                                                                                  #  It may be reasonably asked why tens of thousands of lines of source are joined by
000045,000045:                                                                                                  #  means of inclusion, rather than simply assembling the source files individually and
000046,000046:                                                                                                  #  then linking them to form the executable.  The answer is that the original 
000047,000047:                                                                                                  #  development team had no linker.  The builds were monolithic just like this.
000048,000048:                                                                                                  #  There was a big emphasis on reusability of the code in the original project, 
000049,000049:                                                                                                  #  apparently, but this reusability took the form of inserting your deck of 
000050,000050:                                                                                                  #  punch-cards at the appropriate position in somebody else's deck of punch-cards.
000051,000051:                                                                                                  #  (Actually, I believe a tape-library method was used to avoid having to continually
000052,000052:                                                                                                  #  reload the card decks, but that doesn't change the basic principle.)
000053,000053:                                                                                                  #  So, indeed, the method of file-inclusion is a very fair representation of the 
000054,000054:                                                                                                  #  methods used in the original development ... with the improvement, of course,
000055,000055:                                                                                                  #  that you no longer have to worry about dropping the card deck.  On the other hand, 
000056,000056:                                                                                                  #  I wasn't there at the time, so I may have no idea what I'm talking about.
000057,000057: 
000058,000058:                                                                                                  #  Finally, note that the original Apollo AGC assembler (called "YUL") is no longer 
000059,000059:                                                                                                  #  available (as far as I can tell).  In fact, it was replaced by another assembler
000060,000060:                                                                                                  #  ("GAP") even before Apollo 11, but GAP is no more available than is YUL.  The 
000061,000061:                                                                                                  #  replacement assembler yaYUL accepts a slightly different format for the source 
000062,000062:                                                                                                  #  code from what YUL or GAP accepted, so the source code has been targeted for 
000063,000063:                                                                                                  #  assembly with yaYUL.
000064,000064: 
000065,000065:                                                                                                  #  What follows is simply a bunch of file-includes for the individual code chunks.
000066,000066:                                                                                                  #  I've marked the page numbers to make proof-reading easier.  Besides, the digital
000067,000067:                                                                                                  #  images of the assembly listing contains a lot of interesting tables (cross-
000068,000068:                                                                                                  #  referenced to page numbers) created by GAP, but not duplicated by yaYUL, so it's
000069,000069:                                                                                                  #  still valuable even if the source-files listed below are at hand.
000070,000070:
